et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the siphac with one needle with a strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all four edges together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then bring the needle back to the part where you started, as you sew cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space between each stitch the size of a small finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is known by people,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that a man had on his abdomen,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was caused by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm in size,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and two palms of intestines were protruding,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I put the intestine back after it had been out for 24 hours,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound healed within 15 days, and I treated it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where none were available, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I only placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you about the two specific ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and insert it from the outside part to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the heart straight through, leave the head of the siphac where you inserted the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the inside to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the idea of this stitch is that you sew as the furrier does with skins,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave the siphac on one side once, and take it on the other, until the stitch is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which Galen specifically mentions,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like some do, who join the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and they apply one end of the siphac to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle at the nearest point of the wound, and pierce only that place,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the siphac;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside to the inside,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	with the two ends of the siphac;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make each one pierce from the outside to the inside, on the other side of the wound;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the best and most common manner of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen said this, and some testify,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that one should sew the abdomen with two needles, each with a thread;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should insert one needle on one side and the other on the other side, like those who sew belts;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	the stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with its blood, before it has changed,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put the intestine back, and sew it; then apply the powder that generates flesh,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if it has changed, then apply any available ointment, until the wound opens;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and let the threads fall, and let the siphac and the wound heal;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound like the others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you do not have medicines, then apply, as soon as it starts to discharge, old cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you do not need other medicine in many situations when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound might cause complications to the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary to moisten light wool in oil of moderate heat, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the groin, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if there is pain or decay in the bowels, and it often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then give them an enema with warm dark wine, especially if the decay reaches the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the abundance of veins there, and the delicacy of the whole body, and its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the fat protrudes from the wound, put it back just like the intestine, as long as it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become green or black, it is necessary to tie the place that is black, so that no blood flow reaches it,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ties,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place the two hanging ends from the lower part of the wound to the outside to ease the extraction when the fat falls, and the wound opens.
de la routure dou boueil	Regarding the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some people,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw a man wounded in the abdomen with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it festered and became a fistula, and excrement and gas came out;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it as best I could, and did not stop treating it until it was healed, and the place sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I feared that the patient might have pain in his abdomen;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take ants with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the ant opens its mouth, place it on the two edges,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it clamps its mouth shut;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	then cut off its head, and it holds so that it cannot loosen,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then place another ant afterwards in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	These heads stick to the intestine, and cause no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread made from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread that is well cleaned,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	then tie to the end of this thread a fine twisted linen thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then thread the needle, and sew the intestine, and return it to the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching with ants is only used in cases of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no skill or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Regarding fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes old, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and especially when it is deep and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And fistula is according to its nature a hardened and white scar tissue, where no pain is felt,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is as deep as a bird's feather;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes clear pus comes out, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times a lot;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have already spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is only because of one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is, due to the small amount of blood in the body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its malignancy;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, that does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much pus;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the place is decayed, and the material is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because in that region digestion is slow, and health is slow, and it swells by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must tell you about the cure of fistula done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the membrane, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and some that come to the principal part of the member, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is a fistula that does not reach the place I mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you want to know it, then take a bronze or iron probe, if the fistula is straight, search it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, search it with a fine lead probe,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because lead bends well around the twists;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with probes,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then give it an enema through one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the moisture runs from one opening to another, and cleans it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then search it carefully as best you can, to know if there is bone or nerve, and it is deep,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I mentioned, then cut it as I told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the scar tissue and the decayed flesh inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is very deep in the right place, it is necessary to cut it deeply, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put tents soaked in medicine, and insert them to the end of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine corrodes the excess remaining at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply ointments that generate healthy flesh, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or nerve does not hinder you or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it until all the corruption is removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with things that generate flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, and discharges pus as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone to the bottom:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	so uncover and search until you reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is healed this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other means but to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it with forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	pull it with an appropriate instrument,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, pull them all, do not leave even one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture is against you, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cut both the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then apply to the wound something that generates decay,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the place is decayed around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will be easier to extract;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, like from the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	scrape only the corruption until all the blackness is removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corrupted, and it reaches the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	it is necessary to saw and cut until the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred to a man on his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from inside the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the substances came to the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the doctors by their folly opened the abscess,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings discharged pus and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many doctors treated it for about two years, and there was no one skilled in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines used to treat him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what flowed through the openings with great force;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the young man's body was becoming red, and he had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I placed a probe in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I then hastened, and cut in one of the openings until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption reached the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I sawed what appeared to be the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption, except what I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with healing medicines for a long time, and it could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I started again, and uncovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I sawed it, and then removed it, and tried to heal the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not until I cut around a palm of the bone, and pulled it out with its marrow,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then restored it with medicines; and it healed and sealed quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and did not need to restart the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	Because due to the evacuation he often cried, but he was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard flesh grew in place of the bone, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction at all, neither in walking nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place in the body, it is necessary to saw it in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a strap, and tie it to the end of the exposed bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to stretch it up;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another woolen strap thicker than the first strap, and tie it over the flesh that is over the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the end, so that you pull the corrupted flesh below,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh over the place where you want to saw, so that the saw does not hurt the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a splint or a board under the bone to cut the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to saw as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and saw again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and not visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover all the flesh; then place a splint under,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then saw from one part to the other the corruption, and let the sawing be a little longer than the corruption, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint, and saw the bone where it connects on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the connection of the two joints, there is no other way but to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or the ankle of the foot, it is very difficult,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless it is necessary to inquire about the corrosion, how it appears;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all the ways you can, but make sure the veins or nerves do not contradict you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the cutting instruments and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the setting of the bones and the appearance of the bones,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and delicacy, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare the appropriate instrument for each kind of work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the kinds of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument you need according to what is required.
dou feu	Regarding gangrene
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The flesh rots either due to an internal cause or an external cause;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated that corrosion with medicines, and it does not improve,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	it is necessary to cut that member up to the place where the corrosion reaches,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes death, or the greater harm, which is the loss of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and rots after blackening, then the corrosion goes from member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and spreads throughout the body; so hurry to cut,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is due to the bite of some venomous creatures, like sea scorpion and viper and similar,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the tip of the finger, cut it, and do not allow it to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it reaches the arm, cut it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and no treatment helps except the amount of its strength;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do the same when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut it after the next joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, cut the whole foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up the leg, cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it goes above the knee, there is no other means but to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of cutting or sawing the member is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and one assistant stretches one tie downwards, and another assistant the other tie upwards,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you separate the flesh between the two ties to a spatula's width, until the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or saw it, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the saw does not touch the healthy place,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and does not cause another lesion and hot abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood flow comes when you work, cauterize the place quickly,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then tie the wounded member with an appropriate bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a man with his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness that seemed like a burn from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion first came to his toe, until it covered the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cut the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after the corrosion returned to his finger, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I applied repellent things after cleaning the body, and the corrosion could not be stopped;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut his hand, and I did not want to, as I hoped to repel the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the man's strength was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and hastened to cut his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have told this story so that others may do the same, if needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess occurs in a fleshy place, and stays so long that it gathers a lot of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and pierces, and the pus comes out, and the place remains empty, like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin above it is as thin as a delicate cloth,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it does not reach the bone, nor the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain" (healthy),
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone deeply, it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you cut around that skin, and especially when it is thin, like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not adhere because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you are confident that the skin will adhere, and the corruption is not deep,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a poultice like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	see if the abscess is large, and the pus that comes out is of a foul odor,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then treat it with Egyptian medicine made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take garlic, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put them to cook in a vessel on the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take as much as needed, and melt it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and treat the abscess, and tighten the opening;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the abscess is clean, and the odor is gone;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes it is treated with lye water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not available, and it is that you take ashes from vine wood, and pour water over them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain it, and use it as a poultice, until you know the abscess is well cleaned;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the lye water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then treat it with water and honey where a little crushed litharge is added;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or treat it with honey and mixed wine, as honey has the property to cleanse and wash,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the abscess adhere;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are confident that the abscess is well cleaned,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then treat it with what makes flesh grow in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you take a plaster of diafinit, and melt it with rose oil and in wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or treat it with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned in the treatise on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the abscess is small, and the tube of the poultice cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then widen it a little with an iron, and insert a tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilicon ointment, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then sew it and leave only one place where the poultice can enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening that discharges pus is above, then cut it to a lower place.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the pus is deep, it does not let flesh grow there;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut the abscess below as you wish,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then prepare in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest place it is,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the pus is deep, it does not let flesh grow there
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut the abscess below as you wish,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	then prepare in such a way that the pus flows easily down, and leave nothing of the pus;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put on the abscess,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and spread a linen cloth over it that covers the whole abscess;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut with scissors at the opening of the abscess a little wider than the first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then spread a gentle ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the opening of the abscess to ease the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except once after many days;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and the one that is on the opening of the abscess, remove often to remove the pus,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what flows from the pus, if it is venom or little or much, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been spread in this way and you see the nature rising on the opening of the abscess,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the abscess is adhering, and health is approaching;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change to another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the abscess discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the abscess is not adhering.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venoms flow after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because health is approaching. Because there are men whose flesh growth in their wounds is delayed, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested pus comes out of the abscess after many days, know that the abscess is not adhering;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the abscess is slow to adhere, and is prolonged, then add drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	like diafinit ointment, because it has a large part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diafinit ointment, and melt it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with old wine equally;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then confit it and use it; and the same does well-cooked honey,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when diafinit ointment is not available,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then glue a cloth, and spread it on the abscess, and sometimes administer aristolochia,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lily, which is like flour of vetches and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use it in simple or compound forms: grind them, and make powder, and put it on the honey as I said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption is deep, and affects the bone, or the hard members, or the joints;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	then treat it as a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Regarding the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panaris is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or the foot, or sometimes arises on other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes old, and is not noticed, a hot abscess develops,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and runs and discharges pus until it affects the root of the nail, and sometimes affects the whole nail;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion reaches the bone, causing foul-smelling pain, and the tip of the finger becomes large, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	it is necessary to cut with iron all the excess that remains of the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses the flesh inside, and begins to prick, and injures it,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	it is necessary to put a splint under the nail that pricks the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and push it up, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it, and pull it out, because as long as the corrupted bone is there, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the finger corrupting, cut it at one of the joints as previously mentioned,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is bruised, and swollen, and it feels great pain, it is necessary to bleed it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail with a sharp spatula, cutting across the top,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, because the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, apply something that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the additional finger of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The additional finger that grows on the hands of some people is sometimes all flesh,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes it has bones, and sometimes it has a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them grow at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some joints of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that grow on a joint of the finger do not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that grow at the joint of the finger, sometimes move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cutting of the one that is all flesh is easy, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that grow at the root of the joint are difficult to treat: avoid cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	For those that grow at the last joint, it is necessary to first cut the flesh roundly to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable saw, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The fusion that comes to the fingers together comes by birth, or by fusion of the wound, or by burn, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary to cut that fusion, so that the fingers return to their natural shapes;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between them tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not fuse;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or place between them thin pieces of lead, until the place is healed, as necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the fusion comes to any of these fingers with the palm, cut that fusion as necessary.
Des vils	Of the veins
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Vis are large veins enveloped and full of melancholic excesses, which occur in various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you sometimes administer purgatives for bile, and then treat it with basilica (a type of medicinal herb).
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is done in two ways: one is to cut them and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is to lift the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is done in this manner: first pour very hot water on the leg, until the thick blood is thinned,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then squeeze the patient's leg from above the thigh to below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two or three, with a wide cut,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then elevate and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood flows as the patient's strength can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it, and instruct him to abstain from foods that generate black bile;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The lifting is done in this manner: shave the patient's leg if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath, and pour hot water on his leg until it turns red and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut along the vein from the top of the knee, or the part below at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin with the hook, and strip the vein on each side, until it appears when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it looks red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then put the hook underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then hang it lightly with the hook,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place about three fingers up; then strip the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it with the hook as you did before, and hang it on another hook, as you did the first time;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision, or more if needed, then lift it, and cut it at the toe of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then draw and lift it to the second incision; then extract it from cut to cut, until it comes all out, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw and lift it, insert a needle with a strong double thread,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and draw it, and place a hook underneath, and turn your hand one way and the other, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful it does not break, because if it does, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and it harms the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drawn it all out, place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is twisted and entangled together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	it is necessary to cut it crookedly, but not cut it; and draw it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cut the vein is curved, and does not cut unless it cuts the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of a large curve, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein occurs in the legs, in hot areas where no grass or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and it sometimes appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to decay that comes under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as snakes and worms come within the body, generated between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg with a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes, and the vein begins to emerge, like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head appears, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of lead of one and a half З to two З, and tie it,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the lead hang on the leg, and every time a point comes out, wrap it around the lead, and tie it;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut a part, and wrap the rest, and do not cut it at the root, until it is all out;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it reenters the flesh, and causes an abscess and decay in the place, and bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for which reason it is necessary that it be drawn little by little to the end, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein, when drawn out, is five palms long, or ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a man once came to me, whose vein was ten palms long, and when you cut it, put a hook in the opening, and pierce it to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that it all comes out; and let the matter inside be emptied, and administer medicines generating decay for a few days, then treat it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or on the foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and many openings appear, from which branches come out; treat it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that grow between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often happens to oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, rising and descending,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one can feel it moving from limb to limb, until it tears the skin where it goes, and comes out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is generated from the decay of some humors, just as worms, serpents, lumbrici, and ascarides come in the stomach;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one fears its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	sometimes it reenters and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you want to cure and draw it, you can only do it when it moves:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so it is necessary to tie the place above and below with a strong tight band,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and draw it out, and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you cannot find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	cauterize it with fire on top, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it affects the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming to the head near the eye, press the eyebrow strongly below it, then cut above and draw it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to treat the patient with body purifying medicines for the rotten humors,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and avoid foods that generate decay.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and a little later, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything, like quicksilver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that place, and fixed itself in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later ran through the whole body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me it kept turning around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen many who had seen pain move from place to place,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and exposed veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of that appeared this constrained windiness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear this way in those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you want to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then tie it above and below quickly, and then cut above so that the constrained windiness in the place comes out;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then treat it with what expels windiness, such as fetid pills, and serapinum pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrow wounds are diverse, according to their appearances and the places on the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity among them is that some have large points, small, barbed, and welded;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some have two angles, and others that are long, and some with pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those that fall in any member do so in two ways: either in a principal member,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	it is necessary to avoid extracting this arrow, for death comes afterward in many ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deep, then draw it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls there and pierces the bone, and the membrane over the brain comes out,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	are when there is dizziness and sudden pain and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes blood comes out of the nostrils, or the ears; and sometimes speech and voice are lost;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and white moisture resembling pus comes out of the wound, and also a spray of flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, avoid the cure, and draw the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it falls in the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it is stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood flows, and coldness and cold sweat come, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without doubt that death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that injures the lung are that blood full of foam comes from the wound, the throat swells, the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cool air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls in the covering of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and causes heavy breathing and great pain and sighing; and all the shoulder muscles move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls in the stomach, sometimes some undigested food comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls in the abdomen, and feces come out through the torn intestine, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls in the bladder, and urine flows out and comes externally, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary muscles, spine, buttocks, thigh, and legs, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into the tear duct at the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and drew it from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I drew an arrow from a man whose arrow fell into the fat of the eye under the lower eyelid,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was embedded, and I could only reach the point towards the shaft,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, with a light iron head without barbs; the man was healed, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with barbs:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I sawed off the barbs, and worked carefully until I drew it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew an arrow from a man, who had it fall into his abdomen, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and manipulated it, and drew it out, and no bad accident occurred.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man whose arrow fell into his back, and the wound was sealed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural dispositions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and found no harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, whose arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sealed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and it remained thus without great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I drew an arrow from one of the king's princes, which had fallen into the middle of his nose,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was fully embedded
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the treatment after it had fallen for three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I probed it with a fine probe, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied a drawing and digesting plaster on the place, so that it would not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the place of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained thus for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow one day in his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive liquid medicine on the wound for several days, until it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow that was stuck in the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I added the liquid medicine in the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and about four months passed,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then the wound widened enough that I inserted the forceps, and moved it one way and the other, and it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not stop working carefully and manipulating with various instruments, until one day I took it with well-made forceps,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to its shape that will come at the end of this chapter, until I drew it out, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you apply your treatment to what I do not say, for the book cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise master can infer great things from very little, and from what is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works, and new instruments, to deal with strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of the members where they are stuck except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that comes out through where it enters is an arrow entering fleshy places, and sometimes comes out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out immediately, leave it until the flesh around it rots, and the exit is easier;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce around it with a fine drill, until the place around it is widened, and then draw it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and any of the accidents I have mentioned appear to the patient: do not draw it, but leave it until it is smooth after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow reaches the membrane, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone, and does not reach the membrane,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without bad accidents, then manipulate it to draw it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply stuck and cannot come out, administer drills around it, as I have said; then treat the place until it is healed.
